<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Body_cavities.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1183" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Body_cavities.jpg/300px-Body_cavities.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Body_cavities.jpg/450px-Body_cavities.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Body_cavities.jpg/600px-Body_cavities.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Body_cavities.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Body_cavity" title="Body cavity">Cavities</a> of human body</div></div></div>
<p>Human <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">anatomy</a> is the study of the shape and form of the human body. The human body has four <a href="/wiki/Limb_(anatomy)" title="Limb (anatomy)">limbs</a> (two arms and two legs), a head and a <a href="/wiki/Neck" title="Neck">neck</a> which connect to the <a href="/wiki/Torso" title="Torso">torso</a>. The body's shape is determined by a strong <a href="/wiki/Human_skeleton" title="Human skeleton">skeleton</a> made of <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cartilage" title="Cartilage">cartilage</a>, surrounded by fat (<a href="/wiki/Adipose_tissue" title="Adipose tissue">adipose tissue</a>), muscle, <a href="/wiki/Connective_tissue" title="Connective tissue">connective tissue</a>, organs, and other structures. The <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">spine</a> at the back of the skeleton contains the flexible <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">vertebral column</a> which surrounds the <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a>, which is a collection of nerve fibres connecting the <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a> to the rest of the body. <a href="/wiki/Nerve" title="Nerve">Nerves</a> connect the spinal cord and brain to the rest of the body. All major bones, muscles, and nerves in the body are named, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Anatomical_variation" title="Anatomical variation">anatomical variations</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sesamoid_bone" title="Sesamoid bone">sesamoid bones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accessory_muscle" title="Accessory muscle">accessory muscles</a>.
</p><p>Blood vessels carry blood throughout the body, which moves because of the beating of the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>. <a href="/wiki/Venule" title="Venule">Venules</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vein" title="Vein">veins</a> collect blood low in oxygen from tissues throughout the body. These collect in progressively larger veins until they reach the body's two largest veins, the <a href="/wiki/Superior_vena_cava" title="Superior vena cava">superior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inferior_vena_cava" title="Inferior vena cava">inferior vena cava</a>, which drain blood into the right side of the heart. From here, the blood is pumped into the <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">lungs</a> where it receives oxygen and drains back into the left side of the heart. From here, it is pumped into the body's largest <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">artery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a>, and then progressively smaller arteries and <a href="/wiki/Arteriole" title="Arteriole">arterioles</a> until it reaches tissue. Here blood passes from small arteries into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillaries" title="Capillaries">capillaries</a>, then small veins and the process begins again. Blood carries <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>, waste products, and <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">hormones</a> from one place in the body to another. Blood is filtered at the <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidneys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a>.
</p><p>The body consists of a number of <a href="/wiki/Body_cavity" title="Body cavity">body cavities</a>, separated areas which house different organ systems. The brain and <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> reside in an area protected from the rest of the body by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_brain_barrier" title="Blood brain barrier">blood brain barrier</a>. The lungs sit in the <a href="/wiki/Pleural_cavity" title="Pleural cavity">pleural cavity</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intestine" title="Intestine">intestines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spleen" title="Spleen">spleen</a> sit in the <a href="/wiki/Abdominal_cavity" title="Abdominal cavity">abdominal cavity</a>.
</p><p>Height, weight, <a href="/wiki/Body_shape" title="Body shape">shape</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Body_proportions" title="Body proportions">body proportions</a> vary individually and with age and sex. Body shape is influenced by the distribution of bones, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscle</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fat_tissue" title="Fat tissue">fat tissue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bartleby1918_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-bartleby1918-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physiology">Physiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Physiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_physiology" title="Outline of physiology">Outline of physiology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">Physiology</a></div>
<p>Human <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a> is the study of how the human body functions. This includes the mechanical, physical, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioelectromagnetism" title="Bioelectromagnetism">bioelectrical</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemical</a> functions of humans in good health, from <a href="/wiki/Organ_(biology)" title="Organ (biology)">organs</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a> of which they are composed. The human body consists of many interacting systems of organs. These interact to maintain <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostasis</a>, keeping the body in a stable state with safe levels of substances such as sugar and oxygen in the blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UL_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-UL-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Each system contributes to homeostasis, of itself, other systems, and the entire body. Some combined systems are referred to by joint names. For example, the nervous system and the endocrine system operate together as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neuroendocrine_system" title="Neuroendocrine system">neuroendocrine system</a>. The nervous system receives information from the body, and transmits this to the brain via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nerve_impulse" title="Nerve impulse">nerve impulses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neurotransmitter" title="Neurotransmitter">neurotransmitters</a>. At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Endocrine_system" title="Endocrine system">endocrine system</a> releases hormones, such as to help regulate <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a> and volume. Together, these systems regulate the internal environment of the body, maintaining blood flow, posture, energy supply, temperature, and acid balance (<a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UL_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-UL-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Development_of_the_human_body" title="Development of the human body">Development of the human body</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2657" data-file-width="3986" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg/220px-Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg/330px-Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg/440px-Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Little_baby_from_Puno.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Baby being carried</div></div></div>
<p>Development of the human body is the process of growth to maturity. The process begins with fertilisation, where an egg released from the <a href="/wiki/Ovary" title="Ovary">ovary</a> of a female is penetrated by <a href="/wiki/Sperm" title="Sperm">sperm</a>. The egg then lodges in the <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">uterus</a>, where an <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Fetus" title="Fetus">fetus</a> develop until <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">birth</a>. Growth and development occur after birth, and include both physical and psychological development, influenced by genetic, hormonal, environmental and other factors. Development and growth continue throughout life, through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Childhood" title="Childhood">childhood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">adolescence</a>, and through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adulthood" title="Adulthood">adulthood</a> to <a href="/wiki/Old_age" title="Old age">old age</a>, and are referred to as the process of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aging" title="Aging">aging</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_study">Professional study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Professional study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_anatomy" title="History of anatomy">History of anatomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine" title="History of medicine">History of medicine</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_physiology" title="History of physiology">History of physiology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart,_Lungs,_and_Main_Arteries.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="866" data-file-width="620" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg/170px-Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg/255px-Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg/340px-Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart%2C_Lungs%2C_and_Main_Arteries.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anatomical_Male_Figure_Showing_Heart,_Lungs,_and_Main_Arteries.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Anatomical study by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Health_professional" title="Health professional">Health professionals</a> learn about the human body from illustrations, models, and demonstrations. Medical and dental students in addition gain practical experience, for example by <a href="/wiki/Dissection" title="Dissection">dissection</a> of cadavers. Human anatomy, <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a> are basic medical sciences, generally taught to medical students in their first year at medical school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-introHGray_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-introHGray-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Depiction">Depiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Depiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_figure_(aesthetics)" title="Human figure (aesthetics)">Human figure (aesthetics)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Figure_drawing" title="Figure drawing">Figure drawing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="584" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg/130px-Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg/195px-Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg/260px-Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corinth_stehender_M%C3%A4dchenakt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure drawing by <a href="/wiki/Lovis_Corinth" title="Lovis Corinth">Lovis Corinth</a> (before 1925)</div></div></div>
<p>Anatomy has served the visual arts since Ancient Greek times, when the 5th century BC sculptor <a href="/wiki/Polykleitos" title="Polykleitos">Polykleitos</a> wrote his <i>Canon</i> on the <a href="/wiki/Mathematics_and_art#Polykleitos" title="Mathematics and art">ideal proportions of the male nude</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-67">[67]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a>, artists from <a href="/wiki/Piero_della_Francesca" title="Piero della Francesca">Piero della Francesca</a> (c. 1415–1492) onwards, including <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> (1452–1519) and his collaborator <a href="/wiki/Luca_Pacioli" title="Luca Pacioli">Luca Pacioli</a> (c. 1447–1517), learnt and wrote about the rules of art, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_perspective" title="Visual perspective">visual perspective</a> and the proportions of the human body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_anatomy">History of anatomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: History of anatomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_anatomy" title="History of anatomy">History of anatomy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve,_1543..JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="699" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG/220px-Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG/330px-Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG/440px-Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve%2C_1543..JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Externarvm_hvmani_corporis_sedivm_partivmve,_1543..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two facing pages of text with woodcuts of naked male and female figures, in the <i>Epitome</i> by <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Vesalius" title="Andreas Vesalius">Andreas Vesalius</a>, 1543</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Hippocratic_Corpus" title="Hippocratic Corpus">Hippocratic Corpus</a></i> described the anatomy of the skeleton and muscles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The 2nd century physician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galen_of_Pergamum" title="Galen of Pergamum">Galen of Pergamum</a> compiled classical knowledge of anatomy into a text that was used throughout the Middle Ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritBrit-Galen_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritBrit-Galen-70">[70]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Vesalius" title="Andreas Vesalius">Andreas Vesalius</a> (1514–1564) pioneered the modern study of human anatomy by dissection, writing the influential book <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_humani_corporis_fabrica" title="De humani corporis fabrica">De humani corporis fabrica</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Anatomy advanced further with the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">microscope</a> and the study of the cellular structure of tissues and organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritMicro_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritMicro-73">[73]</a></sup> Modern anatomy uses techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging" title="Magnetic resonance imaging">magnetic resonance imaging</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-ray_computed_tomography" title="X-ray computed tomography">computed tomography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluoroscopy" title="Fluoroscopy">fluoroscopy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_ultrasonography" title="Medical ultrasonography">ultrasound imaging</a> to study the body in unprecedented detail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_physiology">History of physiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: History of physiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_physiology" title="History of physiology">History of physiology</a></div>
<p>The study of human physiology began with <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> in Ancient Greece, around 420 BCE, and with <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> (384–322 BCE) who applied critical thinking and emphasis on the relationship between structure and function. <a href="/wiki/Galen" title="Galen">Galen</a> (ca. 126–199) was the first to use experiments to probe the body's functions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The term physiology was introduced by the French physician <a href="/wiki/Jean_Fernel" title="Jean Fernel">Jean Fernel</a> (1497–1558).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMT_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMT-76">[76]</a></sup> In the 17th century, <a href="/wiki/William_Harvey" title="William Harvey">William Harvey</a> (1578–1657) described the <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system" title="Circulatory system">circulatory system</a>, pioneering the combination of close observation with careful experiment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In the 19th century, physiological knowledge began to accumulate at a rapid rate with the <a href="/wiki/Cell_theory" title="Cell theory">cell theory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Jakob_Schleiden" title="Matthias Jakob Schleiden">Matthias Schleiden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Schwann" title="Theodor Schwann">Theodor Schwann</a> in 1838, that organisms are made up of cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMT_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-NMT-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Claude_Bernard" title="Claude Bernard">Claude Bernard</a> (1813–1878) created the concept of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milieu_interieur" title="Milieu interieur">milieu interieur</a></i> (internal environment), which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_Cannon" title="Walter Cannon">Walter Cannon</a> (1871–1945) later said was regulated to a steady state in <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostasis</a>. In the 20th century, the physiologists <a href="/wiki/Knut_Schmidt-Nielsen" title="Knut Schmidt-Nielsen">Knut Schmidt-Nielsen</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Bartholomew_(biologist)" title="George Bartholomew (biologist)">George Bartholomew</a> extended their studies to <a href="/wiki/Comparative_physiology" title="Comparative physiology">comparative physiology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecophysiology" title="Ecophysiology">ecophysiology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Most recently, <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_physiology" title="Evolutionary physiology">evolutionary physiology</a> has become a distinct subdiscipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_body&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1093669538">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:solid #aaa 1px}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalborder>ul{padding:0.1em;background:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint plainlist portalbox portalborder tright" role="navigation">
